## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the rate of change of concentration (dA/dt) as a function of time and concentration in a chemical reaction. This is a classic chemical kinetics problem where the rate law describes how concentration changes over time, typically following power-law, exponential, or more complex mechanistic rate expressions.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate expression)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reactions)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (combination of first and second order)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (product-catalyzed reaction with stoichiometric constraint)
- Substrate inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (inhibition at high concentration)
- Second-order with saturation: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 / (1 + c1 * A) (transition between orders)
- Consecutive reaction decay: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * exp(c3 * t) (sum of exponential contributions from consecutive steps)
- Power-law with time dependence: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (diffusion-limited or aging kinetics)
- Third-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**3 (termolecular or pseudo-third-order reaction)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with baseline rate)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative proportionality to concentration â†’ first-order decay dA_dt = -k*A, characteristic of radioactive decay or simple decomposition
- Rate proportional to concentration squared â†’ bimolecular reaction mechanism where two molecules of same species collide
- Rate expression as polynomial in A â†’ superposition of parallel reaction pathways of different orders
- Rational function of A (numerator/denominator polynomial) â†’ enzyme-like or surface-catalyzed mechanism with intermediate complex formation
- Product of A and (constant - A) â†’ autocatalytic or logistic-type kinetics where product accelerates reaction
- Exponential time dependence in rate â†’ indicates the system is being driven or has time-dependent rate constants (e.g., photochemical with varying light)
- Sign of dA_dt determines consumption vs production â†’ negative values indicate reactant consumption, positive indicate product formation or autocatalysis
- Non-integer power of A â†’ apparent fractional order suggesting complex mechanism or heterogeneous reaction conditions

**Candidate 82:** `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + c2*exp(c3*t) + c4*log(A*c5 + 1) + c6*exp(c7*t)`

Has `log(A+1)` not `sin(log(A+1))`. No match.

Candidate 82 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 100:** `(A*c0*(c1*exp(c2*t) + 1) + A^c3*c4*(c1*exp(c2*t) + 1) + c5)/(c1*exp(c2*t) + 1)`

= `A*c0 + A^c3*c4 + c5/(c1*exp(c2*t) + 1)`

Needs sin(log(A+1)). No match.

Candidate 100 verdict: [NO MATCH]

Let me look at candidates with both `A*exp(t)` type terms AND `sin(log(A+1))`:

Only Candidate 3 has both `A*exp(c*t)` and `sin(log(A*c+1))`. But as analyzed, it can't produce the standalone `A` term.

Wait, let me re-examine Candidate 3 more carefully:
`A*c0*exp(c1*t) + c2*exp(c3*t) + c4*sin(c5*log(A*c6 + 1) + c7)`

GT = `-0.25667*A - 0.25667*A*exp(-0.02054*t) + 0.94264*sin(log(A + 1))`
   = `-0.25667*A*(1 + exp(-0.02054*t)) + 0.94264*sin(log(A + 1))`

For Candidate 3: We need `A*c0*exp(c1*t) + c2*exp(c3*t)` to equal `-0.25667*A*(1 + exp(-0.02054*t))` = `-0.25667*A - 0.25667*A*exp(-0.02054*t)`.

The term `c2*exp(c3*t)` has no A dependence, so it can't produce `-0.25667*A`. The term `A*c0*exp(c1*t)` can only produce one of the A terms (either the constant one with c1=0 or the exponential one).

So Candidate 3 cannot match. Confirmed.

Now let me think about which structures could work. We need:
- Two terms with factor A (one constant, one with exp(t))
- One sin(log(A+1)) term

Or equivalently: `A * f(t) + sin(log(A+1))` where `f(t) = a + b*exp(c*t)`.

Let me look for candidates with structure like `A*(something with t) + sin(log(A+1))`.

None of the candidates seem to have `sin(log(A+1))` combined with two A-dependent terms.

Let me reconsider candidates with rational structures that might simplify to have the right form.

**Candidate 1:** `(c0*t + c1 + (A*c2 + c3)*(A*c4 + c5*exp(c6*t) + c7*exp(c8*t)))/(A*c2 + c3)`

= `(c0*t + c1)/(A*c2 + c3) + A*c4 + c5*exp(c6*t) + c7*exp(c8*t)`

This has polynomial/rational terms in A and exponentials in t. No sin(log(A+1)). No match.

Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

Let me now systematically go through ALL candidates, focusing on whether they can produce `sin(log(A+1))` or an equivalent nonlinear oscillatory function of A.

- sin(A*c + c): 2, 25, 31, 37, 45, 51, 60, 63, 66, 91, 108, 110, 112, 116, 122, 123, 137, 139, 141, 142
- sin(log(A+c)): 3, 11, 41
- sin(log(t+c)): 88, 93, 98

Candidates with `sin(log(A+c))`: 3, 11, 41 - already checked, none match.

Now, `sin(A*c3 + c4)` â‰  `sin(log(A+1))` for any constants. These are fundamentally different functions. So none of the `sin(A*c+c)` candidates can match.

What about candidates without sin at all? Could any other function equal `sin(log(A+1))`? No - sin(log(A+1)) is an oscillatory function of A that can't be represented by polynomials, exponentials, logs, or power functions.

So the only possible matches must contain `sin(log(A+1))` or equivalent. Only candidates 3, 11, 41 have this, and none matched.

Wait - let me double-check candidate 11 more carefully:
`c0*exp(c1*t) + c2*sin(A*c3 + c4) + c5*sin(c6*log(AÂ²*c7 + 1) + c8)`

Could `sin(c6*log(AÂ²*c7 + 1) + c8)` equal `sin(log(A+1))`? We'd need `c6*log(AÂ²*c7+1) + c8 = log(A+1) + 2Ï€n`. But `log(AÂ²*c7+1)` â‰  `log(A+1)` for any constant c7 (they have different functional forms). No.

Let me reconsider - maybe I should look at this differently. Perhaps some candidates with more complex rational structures could work.

Actually, let me reconsider candidates with the form `(... * (c*exp(t)+1) + extra) / (c*exp(t)+1)` which simplifies to `something + extra/(c*exp(t)+1)`. The term `extra/(c*exp(t)+1)` could potentially give a term proportional to `A*exp(-t)` if extra is proportional to A... but it would be `A/(c*exp(t)+1)` which is NOT `A*exp(-t)`.

Actually, `1/(c*exp(t)+1) = exp(-t)/(c + exp(-t))` which for large c approaches `exp(-t)/c`. But we need EXACT equivalence, not approximations.

Hmm, let me reconsider whether ANY candidate can match. The GT has `sin(log(A+1))` which is a very specific function. Only candidates 3, 11, 41 have anything close, and none can produce all three required terms.
